DO NOT MOVE HERE

I haven't even moved in yet. I put the $100 deposit on an apartment that opens in August 1 month ago and  I am already incredibly unsatisfied and out of $100.

1. When I filled out the application for the apartment and put my $100 deposit I made it clear that I was going to continue to look for another place because I wanted to move in sooner than August. I specifically asked if I would be refunded my $100 if I did find another home. I was told the only thing non-refundable is the $35 credit check.

2. No one disclosed any of the criminal activity that has recently happened at Emerald Pointe to me. Modesto Police Department confirmed that in the last 4 weeks there has be 2 gang related assults, 2 car thefts, and 1 burgulary. How can you feel good about renting to a single mom and her 2 kids and not feel that it is necassary to disclose this kind of information - especially violent crimes.

3. When I called and asked about getting my $100 refunded, the property manager got rude and told me that because my application was already approved she didn't HAVE to give the $100 back - making it sound like she could, but wasn't going to. When I asked if I could talk to her manager she told me she was the manager. When I asked for the information regarding who owns Emerald Pointe she told me she would not disclose that information. WORST COSTUMER SERVICE.

I'm out $100, but at least myself or my family wasn't caught in the crossfire of any criminal activity. You can tell by looking at these apartments that they don't have much to offer - they intice you with the two pools, basketball court, and play ground that you probably wouldn't be safe using. I tried to give them some credit for being under new management but was quickly proven wrong in doing so - these apartments are still the dump everyone says they are. I'm just relieved I found this out prior to moving in.</text>

<Text>I don't live in the area any longer and I used to take my vehicle to "Auto Medics" for many MANY years. They were amazing and sadly closed up shop and moved on. I will miss Chris & Robert.

I'm leaving a review for 4 car garage because of my recent phone conversation with Jennifer. I called the old Auto Medics number (not knowing they closed) and it rang over to 4 Car Garage. I was so confused at first but then found out they'd purchased the customer list and records from Auto Medics. Now hold on there before you start crying foul. They essentially purchased the business. This happens all the time. It just so happens they didn't acquire the physical location though. This is a very smart move because Auto Medics customers were EXTREMELY LOYAL - they knew they could trust the expertise and intentions of Auto Medics.

After spending some time talking with Jennifer about various things (for nearly 45 minutes!) it became very apparent that they are continuing in the exact same manner Auto Medics operated. The same helpful, honest, & knowledgeable professionalism.  Sure wish they were like that where I live now!<//Text>< pictures>

< Review>
Miller Funeral Home first helped us when my mom died in 1995.  We had to ship her out of state for the funeral & burial, but we bought the casket from them and they did the embalming.  They took care of the extra paperwork, made arrangements with the funeral home in Chicago, and made sure we knew what the process was.  Everything was done with kindness and compassion, no stress, no mistakes and they did a beautiful job.  And they didn't try to steer us to the most expensive products, whatever we wanted was fine with them.  So when my mother-in-law died last month, we had already told hospice to contact them.  Irvin picked her up.  He gave us as much time with her as we needed, making sure we didn't feel rushed.  He handled her body with great gentleness and care, as if he loved her as much as my wife and I did.  At the funeral home, Josh helped us with all the paperwork in a kind and loving way and made sure we got the exact urn we wanted.  He returned all my wife's calls promply.  Because of Covid, and because there was no other family here, we didn't have a service at the funeral home.  My wife made a video of a celebration of her life and Josh figured out a way to post it along with her obituary on their website so that family and friends in the rest of the U.S. and Canada could view it.  Mom wanted to be cremated, and it was very comforting to know that they have their own facility for that because we knew we could put our trust in them.  They continue to call and check in on my wife to find out how she is and if they can be of anymore help.  They are the best.<//Review>

<name>Lance Burma<//name><Time>1523304183892</Time><rating>1<//rating>< Review>
We called Esser because they were highly rated on Google. Unfortunately, the experience was a series of failures.

We are new residents in the area and had not called this company before. Our AC was not working and when I called the person who handled the call was very friendly but failed to ask us what kind of system we had. That was their first failure.

We waited until the following afternoon for our appointment.

The next afternoon, the tech arrived just after 5 and was at our place for a couple of hours. He basically, took the panel off the unit and then spent the rest of the time on the phone asking for help from others. He asked us where our air handlers were and when I told him they were in the attic, he told us he was too fat to crawl up there and that "a skinnier guy will have to come out tomorrow." He left without even diagnosing the problem. So, the second failure was sending us an unqualified and apparently out of shape technician.

The next day, I called dispatch at 8:30 in the morning. They had no idea who we were. They eventually found notes on our previous day's call and said that they would be out ASAP. By 1:30, we hadn't heard anything so I called to check on the status and was told that the tech was still on the way. At 3:45, I received a call from dispatch telling me that no one would be coming and that they did not think they could fix our system after all. This call came from their regular dispatch center not someone in management.

So, their third failure was wasting our time for a day and then calling late to say they would not be coming.

Their fourth and final failure was making the poor person in dispatch call and tell us they weren't coming. I would have expected management to take responsibility and make that call themselves.

Top to bottom, our experience with Esser was a complete failure. If you are going to call them, be sure to be specific about the type of equipment you have and be prepared to be patient!

As a post-script, we called another company who sells our particular type of AC unit. They sent a tech out the next day who went up in the attic, reset a switch and had us running in less than 15 minutes.< /Review>

<Name>Gary Westergren< /Name>< Review>
This is a simple Mediterranean (Chaldean) style restaurant. This is family owned and operated, so the mother or son may take your order and serve your food while dad makes the food in the back. They do have a few employees, so that's not always the case.

The food is homemade style. The lentil soup is wonderful. Chicken tikka is very tasty. And the filet mignon is off the charts. The salmon plate is also done just right. I do wish the pita bread was fresh baked. They do heat it up a bit, but if they had a tandoori or brick oven for that, this place would be amazing.</Review>

<user_id>111817572033306577933< /user_id><username>Rex Montefalcon</username>< Date>
1534739455302</Date>
<rating>5<//rating>< Text>
After having gone yesterday for my birthday lunch, the fam and I will definitely be repeat annihilators!!! Being a fan of Middle Eastern/Mediterranean food, I felt the need to give this newly-discovered resto a chance among those that I've given my promiscuous food palette a chance on such as Sahara, Valley Foods, Al Azayem, and North Park Produce.

While the restaurant's location isn't the most appealing (not to their own fault), I thought the owner's made up for it with their interior decor. If it had to be described, I'd say that it was neat, clean, and not too lavish or exotic in theme (which I'd say is a positive).

Their food menu was wall set near the register arranged in side-by-side framery of fairly high-quality, professional appearing culinary photos. The impression I got was that it was an order your food first then sit down type setting...and that we did!

My fam of five opted to go with the meal for three plate that fed our salivating mouths presented on a large silver platter filled with yellow rice (which layered the flat contour of the platter), two beef kebabs, two chicken kebabs, cuts of beef and chicken shawarma, and lastly an extra crispy, golden-brown chicken patty that identically resembled what the Japanese would call chicken katsu.

Now, let me tell you this- I am in no way exaggerating that I have a huge appetite and that portion-size is just as important to me as taste is to practically everyone on this planet aside from a contestant on I guess Naked and Afraid? (shrug). And boy did this place meet the challenge of my stomach's elasticity!!! I'd say it beat it, actually, because we had enough to take home and me to stuff myself with as a midnight snack!

And when we speak of the flavor/taste of the food? Ughhhhhmayzing (amazing)! Each meat item I fed my mouth with was bursting with flavor, no lie! I swear I could taste every fine spice that each food variety in the plate included. I could tell that behind the kitchen door was a cook who poured their love and joy of cooking into the meal that we had that afternoon. And their hummus and baba ganouge that was also served to us was phenomenal as we scooped each kind into neatly cut, fresh and warm from the oven pita bread.

As mentioned earlier, we're definitely coming back as this easily rivals the best I've ever had so far when it comes to Middle-Eastern cuisine (Sahara is my current top choice although I have many restaurants left to try).

Soooo....if you're in the mood for delicious, mouthwatering foodfare, you definitely have to hit this place up if you so happen to get lost in the Casa de Oro neighborhood of the Spring Valley area!

Make sure to give that thumbs up as if you were stranded in the Mojave Desert if you'd like more reviews! :)</Text>

< user_id>
104930705258502539175< /user_id>
<user_name>Bwack Beedows<//user_name><date>1547173450950< /date>< rating>
5< /rating>
< text>
I've been all around California (and the rest the U.S.); this is still the best menudo I can find.

First thing -- most important -- Rosa Maria's restaurant only serves their menudo on the weekend; this is one of the main ways to tell if a business prepares their menudo fresh or simply reheats a frozen stock.

The tripe used is the reticulum section, or "honeycomb", the best type of meat for the stew -- no grease, no gristle. They boil away the fat, ensuring the meat and stock aren't oily and clouded, add the most tender hominy and give it the time it requires to properly stew.

By the time it makes its way to you, this menudo's been properly seasoned and the additional spices and trimmings the staff provide simply make an already amazing dish even more mouthwatering. To top it all off, they'll even add a meaty, tender pork bone, the perfect way to finish off such a satisfying meal.

This place is excellent. Sometimes, the beans have little rocks, but that's just another sign of freshness.

Keep it up, Rosa Maria's! I'll see you next Saturday!< /text>
<pics>None< /pics>< Response>
{'time': 1547229934830, 'text': 'Thank you for your review. Reading it brought a smile to all of our faces here in the Kitchen. All of my staff wants to thank you. We strive to keep our customers happy. We work hard to make sure you only get the freshest and best we can get. We have been working hard for a few months trying to get the Menudo just right. We now know that we hit the nail on the head. Again from our staff thank you.'}<//Response>
